Tiii* enchanting Actress made her first appear	.
ante at this Theatre on Wednesday night, and brought with her those graces of ac tion, person, ami utterance, for which the stage is so infinite!/ indebted to her
It is to us astonishing that a Play like Tit Rivals should ever have met witli any objection from an Audience that, like ours, can discriminate. It is, perhaps, the retort decided proof tc what strange extremes opinions in matters of tmt inav run—a Play, that on its fittt introduction, »■»: nearly hurtl from the Stage, is now the most at tractive of any in the Prompter's list.
And where can be found such colloquial vi vacity—such genuine humour—such refined sen timent, as m this Comedy ; and where also is there to be met with such finished acting as its 'Julia FaUlauJ, hy ha langrnib, and the Absolutet :—1 were neediest to search for it.
Dodd is very entertaining in Arret j anti JDotvi, had more from Bannister than perlw»ps any otht Actor could give.
The Scenery is some of it quite nesv | but . is principally formed from the old flat r, re-tottche by the paintc, and enlarged according to the di menslons of the stage.
The Stage, however, is somewhat contracts and of course the canvas will not be hereafter s expensive an article. We do not approve of tl crimson decoration under the Royal Arens- nor c the ornaments to the stage doors. They do n< at all harmonise with the house, and completcl destroy its effect. Had the colour been light blu this confusion would have been avoided j and t! assimilation witli the • ky and wings would l neater to nature.
